Disney topped expectations with $17.02 billion in revenue and earnings per share of 80 cents. A new Senate bill would totally upend Apple and Google's app store dominance. The Open App Markets Act would enshrine quite quite the quite in the U.S. market for mobile software makers and their customers. The bill would also make it easier for consumers to transfer money from a company's app to a third-party service like Google Play or Apple's App Store. The legislation would also require the companies to disclose how much money they make from their apps, and how much each user spends on them. The act would also allow consumers to opt out of the app store, giving developers more control over how much they make and spend on their products. The Senate bill is expected to be voted on in the coming weeks. It would be the first time the Senate has voted on an app store bill in more than a decade. The measure would be introduced in the spring of next year, and would go into effect in the summer of 2020. It is expected that the Senate will vote on the bill in the fall of this year. The vote would be on whether or not to allow the app stores to take a cut of revenue from the sales of mobile software and services. The company behind the app, Google Play, says the bill would be in the form of a “no-fee” option, allowing the company to charge users a fee for their use of the service. It also said that the fee would be lower if the company agreed to a ‘fair market value’ of $1.5 billion or less. The transaction is valued at approximately $575 million and is set to close in the fourth quarter of 2021 .
